<resp>None</resp>< text>
With all the Chinese restaurants in SF it's tough for a single spot to stand out as better. Came to Golden coast for a birthday dinner and I must admit all of the food was fantastic. I always say if you order the right dishes at Chinese restaurants you'll have a good experience. The seafood soup with shrimp, scallop and bamboo pith was my favorite. Long life lobster noodles, braised pork, and fish and tofu clay pot are great too.< /text>

<user_id>110590184305769403864< /user_id>< text>
A ok did sum spot on ocean Ave. The food is avergae, not bad but not out of this world. You'll almost always get a table here even during the peak times, wait is minimal. Service can be a bit slow, especially if you sit on the second floor. Dinner is a hit of miss, more often good than bad. Once in a while you might get a dish that's too salty or has a weird taste, either due to the freshness of the ingredients or the chef cooking the meal at that time. Overall, if this place is convenient for you, give it a try, but for special occasions, book another place.< /text>

<Date>1567647028014</Date><Rating>5</Rating><text>Dear Endo Sister,

If you're reading this, you've come to the right place! After living with my endometriosis pain and going undiagnosed for almost 20 years, I can honestly say it's worth it and there is hope. Dr. Iris Orbuch gave me my life back.

At 36 years old (less than one year ago), I had given up hope and spent more time on the couch in pain with my heating pad than I did living the active life I loved. I couldn't work full time, got flares when I tried working out or having sex, and was exhausted and in constant pain. No matter how healthy I ate, most foods caused painful bloating. My periods were heavy and lasted 10-14 days every month. I had never struggled with anxiety or depression but withdrew so much from my social life due to pain and exhaustion, that both of those became prevalent. It took a toll on my friendships, relationships with my husband and family, and my emotional wellbeing. I had never felt more alone.

After trying to mentally prepare myself (usually a monthly occurrence pre or post period) that this was the way I'd have to live until I went into menopause, a friend of mine told me about a pelvic floor therapist who then referred to me to Dr. Orbuch. I was so skeptical to see yet another doctor but decided to make an appointment.

As I sat in her waiting room, I couldn't help crying as I read so many women's stories of their journeys and how this doctor has helped them. At that moment I knew I wasn't alone and that I was in exactly the right place.

Five months later I had excision surgery with Dr. Orbuch and within the first week felt better. A weight had been lifted. I wasn't crazy or imagining the pain--lots of endo had been found and removed!

As I write this review, it has been 4 months post surgery and I have been able to resume my active lifestyle pain free! Due to having the disease for so many years and where it was found in my body, I still have a long way to go with physical therapy, regaining strength, maintaining stress levels, and fixing my digestive issues. Physically, mentally, and emotionally I have made a 180 degree turn from where I was at a year ago which is an incredible feeling.

If you are still reading this, know you are not alone and that there is hope and options out there for you. Your life can definitely be regained!

You don't just have surgery and then have to fend for yourself--a plan is set in place to get you to where you need to be to be able to live your best life moving forward! I can't say enough about this amazing woman and the work she is doing to help other women, along with educating healthcare professionals on this painful disease that plagues so many of us.

I want to thank Dr. Orbuch and her team for their amazing support and everything they have done to help me get my life back. The encouragement through the process along with the team of providers pre and post op have been so wonderful.

Thank you!

Love,

< Text>
5 stars for the food.
We have tried most of the Mediterranean food in our area and as far as taste and flavor, it's now one of our favorites.
2 stars for dinner service.
We waited 25 minutes to get the chicken kabob platter and a salad.  I've machine broken and there was only 2 other tables with customers.
This is not a fine dining place that justifies a 25 minute wait.  You order at the counter and the meal is served on styrofoam plates and you clear your own table.  Not a huge deal except for the wait and the tip. FYI 15% is the lowest amount on the iPad screen for a tip.  Next time we will see if there is a no tip option and leave a few bucks at the table, or just call it in.
I can't see making Argos one of our frequent dining options. It's really too bad because it is also close to work and we eat out everyday for lunch.</Text>

Seng Saeliew<//username>
<date>1534766536667<//date><rating>5<//rating><Text>This location is one of my favorite for late night grub spot. There are a few that are along International Blvd. I will go through some of them quickly and what type of scene the spot contains n their specialty.

1. Tacos Mi Rancho
Location: International Blvd n 1st Ave
Scene: Popular with the transient Americans as it doesn't have any of the raunchy scene you would normally encounter with the others. Specialty: Carnitas n Veggie Burrito

2. Taqueria Sinaloa
Locational: International Blvd n 22nd Ave
Scene: Popular w/both the locals n new transient that dwells within the vicinity. Has decent parking, tables n a second truck within feet of each other. Glimpse of working women can be scene in plain sight during the day but more prevalent at night.
Specialty: Shrimp Tacos n overall burrito

3. Mi Grullense Taco Truck
Location: International Blvd n 30th Ave
Scene: Popular with the local Mexicans, Paisa n other Latin group. Good size parking space available compare to the previous scene. Similar raunchy scene of working women can be seen from this location as well. Best to keep to yourself and stay within sight of the Taco truck for your own safety.
Specialty: They are good for their overall menu but on the drier end of the spectrum where it's okay with locals but not for my pallette.

4. Tacos El Gordo
Location: International Blvd n 42nd Ave
Scene: Popular w/lots of locals n heavy traffic scene. Expect long wait especially during the late night when things heat up. Parking can be hectic so plan ahead n bring some drinks while your at it. Party in the back parking lot away from the prying eyes of the police and enjoy your food.
Specialty: Overall good food but the portions tends to be smaller than the other stalls. They make up for it by offering moist n delicious tacos. A lot more pricier than I would have like. The owners have been inflating the price for the last 3-4 years. The reason is for this is to fund their other new location while retaining their profit quotas.

5. El Taco Zamorano
Location: International Blvd n High St. Their other location is a few blocks down on 48th Ave.
Scene: Pretty much a dead scene for the most part.
Specialty: There isn't anything that really stands out on this scene. This is the definition of meh quality where it just is a waste of your time. Parking is limited and this also deters a bit of traffic from coming through.

6. Tacos Guadalajara
Location: International Blvd n 44th Ave
Scene: Hidden gem with the locals w/enough parking. The outside place has been remodeled w/seating n good lighting. The views however is dead as the location is on the farther end of the International Blvd where not too many venture to. It's also only fees away from a halfway house so beggers are a common scene here. Other than the usual asking for hand out...they usually do not bother the patrons.
Specialty: This place is considered the second best options to going to El Gordo and I really do wish that they will catch on in time in offering home grilled serrano peppers versus can jalape√±os from the store. It really makes a big difference...the cost is little but the difference is huge. Hopefully they are reading this.

Tacos Guadalajara is my favorite scene as it tends to be quite and I can enjoy my meal out of of trunks while just minding my own business. If I'm with my friends n the night is still young then no doubt I will be over at El Gordo w/a bottle of Hennessey and 20 tacos for the friends n I.<//Text>< Pics>

<userid>116841262733993359192<//userid>< Name>
Matthew Griesinger<//Name>
<pictures>None</pictures><review>I recently went to Evans Vista to get an oil change for my wife's car. Normally I go to San Marcos, but I was at my parent's house in Carlsbad and Vista was closer.

I cannot say I will ever go back to Evans Vista.

1) At Evan's San Marcos, my oil change out the door price is usually around $48 after coupon. At Evan's Vista, the price seemed a little high, but I did not have my old paperwork with me to remind me how much I usually pay. Upon my being able to check my previous service receipts, I was normally charged ~$48 (going back to 2017) for synthetic oil changes at Evan's San Marcos (after discount), and at Evan's Vista, they charged me $74 out the door (after discount). I do not know what was different (Per the receipt, Valvoline Oil Syn Oil was different), but I felt a little cheated at the price charged post discount at Evan's Vista (especially since PepBoys across the street was $75 -$20 web discount for a synthetic oil change). This was not a deal-breaker, because I should have been more prepared and questioned the high quote, but it was disappointing for me. In the future, I am going to call ahead and get an "out-the-door" quote. (minus one star)

2) I was called and told that my shocks/struts were overdue and bad. Evan's Vista told me my tires showed signs of cupping, my shocks/struts were bad, and that one of the rear shocks/struts were leaking. I told Evan's Vista I had my shocks/struts replaced less than 30k miles ago at a different repair shop and that they should not be showing much wear.
